Void Conditions in the Appointment of a Governor (Imarah)
Ruling on void conditions in appointment of a governor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on void conditions in the appointment of a governor and explain why the appointment remains valid.

Core Idea
A void condition in a governor's appointment does not invalidate the appointment itself.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding conditions attached to the appointment of a governor (imarah). The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that if a caliph imposes a condition unrelated to the office — such as requiring the governor to ride — the condition is void but the appointment remains fully valid. This illustrates a broader Hanafi principle that a void condition in a contract of public office does not nullify the contract, unlike certain other contracts where a void condition may render the contract void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the appointment of a governor (imarah). The ruling is that the appointment is valid (sahih) even if a void condition is attached.
This is based directly on the text's statement: 'wa la tabtulu imaratuhu bidha' (his governorship is not invalidated by it).
2
Identify the condition and its validity
The condition given is 'on condition that you ride.' Since riding is unrelated to the office's duties, the condition is void (fasid).
The condition is not fulfilling a necessary purpose of the office.
3
Determine the effect of the void condition
According to the Hanafi school, a void condition in a public office appointment does not invalidate the contract. The appointment remains in force and only the condition is ignored.
This ruling is specific to contracts of wilayah (authority); in sales, a void condition may invalidate the contract.
4
Note the lexical and hadith context
The author clarifies the meaning of imarah and cites a hadith warning against desiring authority, but these do not alter the legal ruling.
The hadith serves as a moral lesson, not a legal proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والامارة) بأن قال الخليفة وليتك إمارة الشام مثلاً على أن تركب فهذا الشرط فاسد ولا تبطل أمريته بهذا. والإمارة مصدر كالإمرة بالكسر . يقال فلان أمر وأمر عليه إذا كان والياً وقد كان سوقه أي أنه يجرب والتأمير تولية الإمارة يقال هو أمير مؤمر وتأمر عليهم أي تسلط؛ كذا في الصحاح. وفي صحيح البخاري إنكم ستحرصون على الإمارة وستكون ندامة. القيامة» (۱) قوله : (والكفالة بأن قال كفلت غريمك إن أقرضتني، كذا ذكره العيني.
His saying: (And governorship) that the caliph says, 'I appoint you governor of Syria, for example, on condition that you ride,' so this condition is void, and his governorship is not invalidated by it. And imarah is a verbal noun like imrah with kasrah. It is said: so-and-so amara and amara 'alayhi if he was a governor, and 'sawqahu' means he tests, and ta'mir is appointment to governorship. It is said: he is ameer mu'ammar, and ta'mara 'alayhim means he dominated. This is as in al-Sihah. And in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'You will be eager for governorship, and it will be a regret on the Day of Resurrection.' Then his saying: (And suretyship) that he says, 'I am surety for your debtor if you lend me,' as mentioned by al-Ayni.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This short passage deals with conditions in the appointment of a governor (imarah). The author gives an example: the caliph says, 'I appoint you governor of Syria on condition that you ride.' This condition (presumably meaning you must ride a horse or use a mount) is void (fasid) because it is not relevant to the office, but the appointment itself remains valid; the governorship is not invalidated by such a trivial condition. The author then provides lexical notes on the word 'imarah' and quotes a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari warning against excessive desire for authority. The text then transitions to the next topic (suretyship).

Key Terms
إمارة (imarah): Governorship; the office of a regional ruler or governor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a caliph appoints a governor on condition that the governor ride a horse, what is the ruling on the appointment?
A) The appointment is void because the condition is void.
B) The appointment is valid and the condition is binding.
C) The appointment is valid but the condition is void.
D) The appointment is suspended until the condition is fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
A void condition in a public office appointment does not invalidate the appointment; the condition is ignored and the office continues.

Valid and Invalid Conditions in Agency (Wakalah)
Rules on conditional agency and void conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid conditions in a wakalah contract and state the Hanafi ruling on void conditions.

Core Idea
Suspending the agency itself on a condition is valid; suspending removal on a condition is invalid.

In Hanafi fiqh, agency (wakalah) can be made conditional, but the law distinguishes between conditions that affect the appointment and those that affect its termination. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that while suspending the appointment of an agent on a condition (e.g., 'I appoint you if you forgive my debt') is permissible, attempting to suspend the removal of an agent (e.g., 'You are removed if you do not sell') renders the condition invalid. Moreover, even if a condition is void, the agency itself remains valid and enforceable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule on conditional agency
Note that the Hanafi school permits suspending the agency contract itself on a condition. The condition must be valid in itself (e.g., discharging a debt).
The example given: 'I appoint you as agent if you discharge me from your claim.'
2
Examine the distinction between appointment and removal
Suspending the appointment (tawkeel) on a condition is valid, but suspending the removal (azl) on a condition is invalid. Appreciate the asymmetry: removal must be unconditional.
From al-Bazzaziyyah: تعليق الوكالة بالشرط جائز وتعليق العزل به باطل.
3
Analyze the two corollaries given
If the principal says 'Whenever I remove you, you are my agent' or 'Whenever I appoint you, you are removed,' both are invalid. The first tries to negate removal, the second tries to condition removal on appointment.
These are invalid because they attempt to condition removal or make removal ineffective.
4
Apply the overarching rule on void conditions
Even if a condition is void (fāsid), the agency contract itself remains valid. The void condition is simply ignored.
Al-Bazzaziyyah: الوكالة لا تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والوكالة بأن قال وكلتك إن أبرأتني عما لك علي؛ ذكره العيني. وهو مثال تعليقها بالشرط وفي البزازية : تعليق الوكالة بالشرط جائز وتعليق العزل به باطل وتفرع على ذلك أنه قال كلما عزلتك فأنت وكيلي أنه لأنه تعليق التوكيل بالعزل، وسيأتي طريق عزله، ولو قال كلما وكلتك فأنت معزول لم يصح لأنه تعليق العزل بالشرط وفي البزازية الوكالة لا تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة أي شرط كان
His saying: (And agency) that he says, 'I appoint you as agent if you discharge me from what you have against me'; mentioned by al-Ayni. This is an example of suspending it upon a condition. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: Suspending agency upon a condition is valid, and suspending its termination upon a condition is invalid. Derived from that: if he says, 'Whenever I remove you, you are my agent,' it is invalid because it is suspending appointment upon removal, and the method of his removal will come. And if he says, 'Whenever I appoint you, you are removed,' it is not valid because it is suspending termination upon a condition. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: Agency is not invalidated by void conditions, whatever the condition.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage deals with conditions in agency (wakalah). The author gives an example of suspending the agency on a condition: 'I appoint you as agent if you discharge me from your claim.' This is a valid conditional agency. From al-Bazzaziyyah: suspending the agency itself on a condition is valid, but suspending the removal of the agent on a condition is invalid. For example, if the principal says, 'Whenever I remove you, you are still my agent,' this is invalid because it tries to make removal ineffective. Similarly, 'Whenever I appoint you, you are removed' is also invalid because it attempts to terminate the agency by the same act of appointment. However, agency is not invalidated by any void condition; the condition is void but the agency remains valid.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakalah): Agency; a contract where one person authorizes another to act on his behalf.
عزل (azl): Removal or termination of an agent or appointee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a principal says: 'I appoint you as agent if you forgive my debt'?
A) The agency is invalid because it is conditional.
B) The agency is valid and the condition is binding.
C) The agency is valid as a conditional appointment.
D) The agency is suspended until the condition is fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
Suspending the agency on a condition is valid, but suspending removal on a condition is invalid, and void conditions do not affect the validity of the agency.

Valid Conditions in Kitabah
Ruling on valid conditions in kitabah contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a condition in kitabah restricting the slave's movement is valid and distinguish it from a suspended condition.

Core Idea
A condition in kitabah restricting the slave's movement is valid and does not void the contract.

In the Hanafi school, conditions within a kitabah contract are generally permitted as long as they do not contradict the essence of the contract. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a concrete example: the master stipulates that the slave not leave the city. Such a condition is considered a valid stipulation (shart sahih), not a suspension (ta'liq), and thus the kitabah remains valid. This lesson unpacks this ruling and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the condition
The contract is kitabah (mukatabah) where a slave purchases freedom in installments. The master adds a condition: the slave must not leave the city.
2
Classify the condition
Determine whether the condition is a suspension (ta'liq) or a mere condition (shart). The author explicitly states it is not a suspension but a valid condition.
A suspension would make the contract contingent on a future event; here the condition is attached as a stipulation.
3
State the ruling
The condition is valid (sahih) and does not invalidate the kitabah contract. The kitabah remains in effect with the condition binding on the slave.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
4
Apply to practice
If the slave violates the condition (e.g., leaves the city), the master may have remedies, but the contract itself was valid from inception.
The breach of condition does not retroactively void the kitabah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والكتابة) بأن قال المولى لعبده كاتبتك على ألف بشرط أن لا تخرج من البلد أو اشتراط الخيار للمحتال في كون ذلك من التعليق نظر بل هو شرط لكنه صحيح ليس مما نحن فيه تأمل . قوله : (وهذه واردة على إطلاق المصنف وغيره قال في النهر وجوابه أن هذا من المحتال وعد وليس الكلام فيه اهـ. ومراده من المحتال المحتال عليه لأنه قد تحذف صلته، وهذا الجواب غير ظاهر عن هذا لأن كونه وعداً لا يخرجه عن كونه شرطاً . قوله : (وأما ما ذكر) أي من قول العيني أقلتك البيع إن أقرضتني كذا ومراد المؤلف الاعتراض على العيني بأن المراد بيان ما لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد، وما ذكره من المثال تعليق بالشرط والتعليق بالشرط لا . كما يصح ذكره في القنية. وذكر المؤلف في آخر باب الإقالة أن فائدة كون الإقالة فسخاً تظهر في خمس مسائل : الثانية منها أنها لا تبطل بالشروط المفسدة ولكن لا يصح تعليقها بالشرط كأن باع ثوراً من زيد فقال اشتريته رخيصاً فقال زيد إن وجدت مشترياً بالزيادة فبعه منه فوجد فباع بأزيد لا ينعقد البيع الثاني لأنه تعليق الإقالة لا الوكالة
His saying: (And kitabah) that the master says to his slave, 'I have contracted kitabah with you for a thousand on condition that you do not leave the city' or stipulating an option for the creditor (muhtal) — regarding that being a suspension, there is consideration; rather it is a condition, but it is valid and not our topic here. Reflect. His saying: (And these [examples] contradict the absolute statement of the author and others) — he said in al-Nahr: The answer is that this is a promise from the muhtal and the discussion is not about it. And his meaning by muhtal is the muhtal 'alayh (transferee), because its relation may be omitted. And this answer is not apparent because being a promise does not remove it from being a condition. His saying: (And as for what was mentioned) meaning from the saying of al-Ayni, 'I rescind the sale from you if you lend me' — the author intends to object to al-Ayni that the intent is to explain what is not invalidated by a void condition, and what he mentioned is a suspension by condition, and suspension by condition is not valid, as mentioned in al-Qunyah. And the author mentioned at the end of the chapter on iqalah that the benefit of iqalah being a rescission appears in five issues: the second of them is that it is not invalidated by corrupting conditions, but its suspension by a condition is not valid. For example, if he sold an ox to Zayd and said, 'I bought it cheap,' and Zayd said, 'If you find a buyer at a higher price, sell it to him,' and he found and sold at a higher price, the second sale is not concluded because it is a suspension of iqalah, not agency.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage addresses conditions in kitabah (a contract where a slave purchases his freedom by paying installments). The author gives an example: the master says, 'I contract kitabah with you for a thousand on condition that you not leave the city.' Here, the condition is not a suspension of the contract but a condition within it. The ruling is that such a condition is valid (the kitabah is valid) but the condition itself may be subject to discussion. However, the author notes that this condition is not a suspension (ta'liq) but rather a condition (shart) that does not affect the contract's validity. The rest of the passage is actually a continuation of the iqalah discussion, clarifying that the examples given by al-Ayni are suspensions and thus invalid for iqalah, but the author's point is about conditions that do not invalidate the contract. The example of the ox and the second sale illustrates that if someone says, 'If you find a buyer at a higher price, sell it to him,' this is a suspension of iqalah (i.e., a conditional rescission) which is invalid; the second sale does not take effect because it is not a valid agency either.

Key Terms
كتابة (kitabah): A contract of manumission where a slave pays a sum to the master in installments to earn freedom.
شرط صحيح (shart sahih): A valid condition that does not invalidate the contract and is binding on the parties.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension; making the contract contingent on a future event.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a kitabah contract, if the master stipulates that the slave not leave the city, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The condition is void and the kitabah is invalid.
B) The condition is valid and the kitabah remains valid.
C) The condition is a suspension and invalidates the contract.
D) The contract becomes suspended until the condition is removed.

Key Takeaway
A condition in kitabah that restricts the slave's movement is valid and does not invalidate the contract.

Definition, Pillar, and Conditions of Sarf
Defines Sarf linguistically and legally, states its pillar, and lists four conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sarf, identify its pillar, and list the four conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Sarf is the sale of currencies; its validity hangs on immediate possession, no option, no deferment, and weight equality for same genus.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq defines sarf and outlines its four essential conditions. Understanding these conditions is crucial because they apply to all currency exchanges, including modern foreign exchange. The passage begins by explaining the linguistic meaning before giving the legal definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
The author states: 'Sarf is the sale of some of the prices (athman) for others.' Note that 'prices' means gold and silver currency, including manufactured items that are no longer pure thaman.
The definition is broad enough to include jewelry exchanged for cash.
2
Distinguish linguistic and legal meanings
The passage gives linguistic meanings from Qamus and Sihah (increase, exchange, etc.) then moves to the legal definition which is narrower and specific to currency exchange.
Linguistic meaning is broader; legal meaning is technical.
3
State the pillar
The pillar (rukn) of sarf is the same as any sale: offer and acceptance (ijab wa qabul) or mutual handing (ta'ati).
No special pillar beyond the general sale contract.
4
List the four conditions
Identify each condition from the text: (1) possession of both counter-values before physical separation, (2) the contract must be binding with no option (except defect and sight options), (3) no deferment (mu'ajjal), (4) equality in weight if the same genus (e.g., gold for gold).
These conditions are derived from the hadith 'sell gold for gold hand to hand, equal for equal.'
5
Recognize exceptions and details
The author notes that defect option and sight option are allowed; deferment can be revoked before separation to make the contract valid.
These details affect the practical application of the conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الصَّرْفِ هُوَ بَيْعُ بَعْضِ الْأَثْمَانِ بِبَعْضٍ فَلَوْ تَجَانَسَا شَرْطُ التَّمَاثُلِ وَالتَّقَابُضِ وَإِنِ اخْتَلَقًا جَوْدَةً تَقَدَّمَ وَجْهُ تَأْخِيرِهِ وَالْكَلَامُ فِيهِ فِي مَوَاضِعَ: الْأَوَّلُ فِي مَعْنَاهُ اللُّغَوِيِّ. ذُكِرَ فِي الْقَامُوسِ أَنَّ صَرْفَ الْحَدِيثِ أَنْ يُزَادَ فِيهِ وَيُحَسَّنَ مِنَ الصَّرْفِ فِي الدَّرَاهِمِ وَهُوَ فَضْلُ بَعْضِهِ عَلَى بَعْضٍ فِي الْقِيمَةِ وَكَذَلِكَ صَرْفُ الْكَلَامِ. وَأَمَّا الصَّرْفُ فِي الْحَدِيثِ «لَا يَقْبَلُ اللَّهُ مِنْهُ صَرْفًا وَلَا عَدْلًا» فَالصَّرْفُ التَّوْبَةُ وَالْعَدْلُ الْفِدْيَةُ أَوْ هُوَ النَّافِلَةُ وَالْعَدْلُ الْفَرِيضَةُ أَوْ بِالْعَكْسِ، أَوْ هُوَ الْوَزْنُ وَالْعَدْلُ الْكَيْلُ، أَوْ هُوَ الِاكْتِسَابُ وَالْعَدْلُ الْفِدْيَةُ أَوِ الْحِيَلُ. وَفِي الصِّحَاحِ: يُقَالُ صَرَفْتُ الدَّرَاهِمَ بِالدَّنَانِيرِ وَبَيْنَ الدِّرْهَمَيْنِ صَرْفٌ أَيْ فَضْلُ الْجَوْدَةِ فِضَّةُ أَحَدِهِمَا عَلَى الْآخَرِ. وَالثَّانِي فِي مَعْنَاهُ فِي الشَّرِيعَةِ وَقَدْ أَفَادَهُ بِقَوْلِهِ قَوْلُهُ: (هُوَ بَيْعُ بَعْضِ الْأَثْمَانِ بِبَعْضٍ) كَالذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ إِذَا بِيعَ أَحَدُهُمَا بِالْآخَرِ أَيْ بَيْعُ مَا مِنْ جِنْسِ الْأَثْمَانِ بَعْضِهَا بِبَعْضٍ. وَإِنَّمَا فَسَّرْنَاهُ بِهِ وَلَمْ نُبْقِهِ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ لِيَدْخُلَ فِيهِ بَيْعُ الْمَصُوغِ بِالْمَصُوغِ أَوْ بِالنَّقْدِ فَإِنَّ الْمَصُوغَ بِسَبَبِ مَا اتَّصَلَ بِهِ مِنَ الصِّنْعَةِ لَمْ يَبْقَ ثَمَنًا صَرِيحًا وَلِهَذَا يَتَعَيَّنُ فِي الْعَقْدِ ذَلِكَ بَيْعُهُ صَرْفٌ. الثَّالِثُ فِي رُكْنِهِ فَمَا هُوَ رُكْنُ كُلِّ بَيْعٍ فَهُوَ رُكْنُهُ مِنَ الْإِيجَابِ وَالْقَبُولِ أَوِ التَّعَاطِي. وَالرَّابِعُ فِي شَرَائِطِهِ فَأَرْبَعَةٌ: الْأَوَّلُ قَبْضُ الْبَدَلَيْنِ قَبْلَ الِافْتِرَاقِ بِالْأَبْدَانِ. الثَّانِي أَنْ يَكُونَ بَاتًّا لَا خِيَارَ فِيهِ فَإِنْ شَرَطَ فِيهِ خِيَارَ وأَبْطَلَهُ صَاحِبُهُ قَبْلَ التَّفَرُّقِ صَحَّ وَبَعْدَهُ لَا. وَأَمَّا خِيَارُ الْعَيْبِ فَثَابِتٌ فِيهِ، وَأَمَّا خِيَارُ الرُّؤْيَةِ فَثَابِتُ فِي الْعَيْنِ دُونَ الدِّينِ. وَإِذَا رَدَّهُ بِعَيْبٍ انْفَسَخَ الْعَقْدُ، سَوَاءً رَدَّهُ فِي الْمَجْلِسِ أَوْ بَعْدَهُ، وَإِنْ كَانَ دَيْنًا فَرَدَّهَا فِي الْمَجْلِسِ لَمْ يَنْفَسِخْ، فَإِذَا رَدَّ بَدَلَهُ بَقِيَ الصَّرْفُ وَإِنْ رَدَّ بَعْدَ الِافْتِرَاقِ بَطَلَ، وَتَمَامُهُ فِي الْبَدَائِعِ. الثَّالِثُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ بَدَلُ الصَّرْفِ مُؤَجَّلًا فَإِنْ أَبْطَلَ صَاحِبُ الْأَجَلِ الْأَجَلَ قَبْلَ التَّفَرُّقِ وَنَقَدَ مَا عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ افْتَرَقَا عَنْ قَبْضٍ مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنِ انْقَلَبَ جَائِزًا وَبَعْدَ التَّفَرُّقِ لَا. الرَّابِعُ التَّسَاوِي فِي الْوَزْنِ إِنْ كَانَ الْمَعْقُودُ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ جِنْسٍ وَاحِدٍ.
The Book of Sarf: It is the sale of some of the prices for others. If they are of the same genus, then equality and hand-to-hand possession are conditions, even if they differ in quality. The discussion on it has aspects: first, its linguistic meaning...
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Sarf (currency exchange). The author first gives the legal definition from the matn: Sarf is the sale of one type of medium of exchange (thaman) for another. He then clarifies that this includes both pure metals and manufactured items (like jewelry) that are no longer pure thaman. The pillar (rukn) of Sarf is the same as any sale: offer and acceptance or mutual handing. The four conditions are then listed: (1) possession of both counter-values before physical separation, (2) the contract must be binding with no option (except defect option and sight option in certain cases), (3) the exchange cannot be deferred, (4) if the same genus (e.g., gold for gold), equality in weight is required. These conditions are derived from the hadith 'sell gold for gold hand to hand, equal for equal.' The author provides brief rulings on options and delayed payment, noting that if a condition is voided before separation, the contract can become valid. This is a foundational passage for understanding Sarf.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): Sale of one type of thaman (currency) for another; also a linguistic term for increase or exchange.
أثمان (athman): Prices or media of exchange, primarily gold and silver coinage, but also includes manufactured items that are not pure thaman.
تقابض (taqābuḍ): Mutual physical taking possession of the counter-values before the parties separate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Possession of both counter-values before separation
B) The contract must be binding with no option
C) The exchange can be deferred
D) Equality in weight if the same genus

Key Takeaway
Sarf is a special sale with strict conditions: immediate possession, no option, no deferment, and weight equality for same genus.

Post-Contract Increase and Reduction in Sarf: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on post-contract adjustments in Sarf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why post-contract increases of the same genus in Sarf corrupt the original contract according to Abu Hanifa, and distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
A post-contract excess of the same genus in Sarf corrupts the original contract according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn differ.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the conditions of equality and hand-to-hand possession in Sarf, then presents a famous intra-Hanafi dispute: when one party gives an increase or reduction after the contract is concluded, does the original contract remain valid? Abu Hanifa's ruling is that it becomes corrupt, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad offer alternative views. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to trace the thamarah al-khilaf in real transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? A Sarf contract (exchange of gold/silver). According to Abu Hanifa, what is the effect of a post-contract increase of the same genus? The original contract becomes corrupt (fasid).
2
Locate the points of disagreement
Identify the three positions: Abu Hanifa says original corrupt; Abu Yusuf says original valid but increase/reduction void; Muhammad says increase void but reduction valid as an independent gift.
3
Trace the underlying principle
The disagreement stems from whether a fasid condition mentioned after the contract attaches to it. Abu Hanifa says it does, corrupting the contract; the Sahibayn say it does not (or only partially).
This principle is the core usul question behind the ikhtilaf.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a buyer gives extra gold after the exchange, Abu Hanifa requires a new valid contract; under the Sahibayn, the original may stand but the excess is void.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities prefer Abu Hanifa's view, so the operative ruling is that the original contract becomes fasid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن علم التساوي الخ) وفي الكفاية : العلم بتساويهما حالة العقد شرط صحته حتى لو تبايعا ذهباً بذهبٍ أو فضة بفضة مجازفة لم يجز، فإن علما التساوي في المجلس وتفرقا عن قبض صح. وكذا لو اقتسما الجنس مجازفة لم يجز إلا إذا علم التساوي في المجلس لأن القسمة كالبيع. كذا في السراج الوهاج. قوله : (فلو تجانسا شرط التماثل والتقابض) أي النقدان بأن أحدهما بجنس الآخر. ومن قبض البدلين قبل الافتراق. أما التساوي فقدمناه. فرع: في باب الربا ولو تصارفا جنساً بجنس مثلاً بمثل وتقابضا وتفرقا ثم زاد أحدهما صاحبه شيئاً أو حط عنه شيئاً وقبله الآخر فسد البيع عند أبي حنيفة، وعند أبي يوسف هما باطلان والصرف صحيح، وعند محمد الزيادة باطلة والحط جائز بمنزلة الهبة المستقلة. واختلافهم هذا اختلافهم في أن الشرط الفاسد المتأخر عن العقد في الذكر إذا ألحق به هل يلتحق أم لا؛ فمن أصل أبي حنيفة التحاقه ويفسد العقد ومن أصلهما التحاقه فطرده أبو يوسف هنا، ومحمد فرق بين الزيادة والحط. ولو زاد أو حط في صرف بخلاف الجنس جاز إجماعاً لكن يشترط قبض الزيادة قبل الافتراق لالتحاقها بأصل العقد. ولو حط مشتري الدينار قيراطاً منها فبائع الدينار يكون شريكاً له في الدينار. ولو زاد مشتري السيف المحلى ديناراً جاز، ولا يشترط قبضه قبل الافتراق لصرف الزيادة إلى النصل والحمائل وتمامه في البدائع.
His saying: 'If equality is known...' etc. In al-Kifayah: knowledge of their equality at the time of contract is a condition of its validity...
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage delves into two conditions: equality (tamathul) and mutual possession (taqabud). First, the author explains that for same-genus Sarf, equality must be known at the time of contract; conjectural equality is insufficient. If both parties know, then separate after possession, it is valid. Then he discusses the famous intra-Hanafi dispute: after a valid Sarf contract, if one party later gives an increase (ziyada) or reduction (hatt) to the other, what happens? Abu Hanifa holds that the original contract becomes corrupt because the defective condition attaches retroactively. Abu Yusuf says both the increase and the original contract are void, but the Sarf itself is valid. Muhammad distinguishes: the increase is void, but the reduction is valid as an independent gift. This disagreement is rooted in the principle of whether a later defective condition attaches to the contract. Abu Hanifa says it does. The passage also covers cases where the increase is of a different genus (unanimously allowed) and the unique case of a sword with a gold hilt, where the increase attaches to the blade, not to the gold exchange.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyāda): Increase given by one party to the other after the Sarf contract is concluded.
حط (ḥaṭṭ): Reduction or remission of part of the debt or counter-value in a Sarf contract.
شرط فاسد (sharṭ fāsid): A condition that is legally invalid, such as an increase that creates riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the effect on the original Sarf contract if one party gives an excess of the same genus after separation?
A) The contract becomes fasid (corrupt)
B) The contract remains valid but the excess is void
C) The contract remains valid and the excess is a gift
D) Both the contract and the excess are void

Key Takeaway
The effect of a post-contract increase or reduction in Sarf depends on the genus and the imam; per the mufta bihi (Abu Hanifa), any such adjustment of the same genus corrupts the original contract.

Possession and Separation in Sarf: Hand-to-Hand Requirement
Defines hand-to-hand possession and bodily separation in Sarf with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of mutual physical possession before bodily separation in Sarf contracts and apply it to scenarios involving agents, messengers, and the father-minor son exception.

Core Idea
Sarf requires hand-to-hand delivery before the parties' bodies separate—physical togetherness, not location, defines the contract's closure.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the essential condition of possession (qabd) and separation (iftiraq) in Sarf contracts. The author clarifies that separation means bodily separation, not leaving the sitting place, and explores several derived cases including agents, messengers, and the exceptional case of a father transacting with his minor son. Understanding these details prevents common errors when applying the pivotal hadith of 'gold for gold, hand to hand.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition
State the requirement: mutual physical possession must occur before the parties separate by their bodies.
The Arabic term is taqābuḍ qabla al-iftirāq bil-abdān.
2
Analyze the definition of separation
Understand that walking together, even a mile, does not constitute separation. Separation only occurs when one body leaves the other.
Iftirāq bil-abdān is strict; even signs of aversion (i'rād) do not invalidate the contract.
3
Examine the derived rulings
Work through the examples: messenger contract (void because principal and counterparty are separated), calling from behind a wall (void), and agents (each agent's share stands independently).
For agents, possession must occur for each share before the respective agent separates.
4
Recognize the exception
Note the father-minor son case: when physical separation is impossible (child in father's custody), the sitting (majlis) is considered instead of bodies.
This is a ruling from Imam Muhammad, preserved in al-Asl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما التقابض فالمراد التقابض قبل الافتراق بأبدانهما بأن يأخذ هذا في جهة وهذا في جهة، فإن مشيا ميلاً أو أكثر ولم يفارق أحدهما صاحبه فليسا بمتفرقين. ولا يبطل بما يدل على الأعراض بخلاف خيار المخيرة فإنه يبطل بما يدل عليه. وتفرع على ما ذكرناه أنه لو كان لكل من رجلين على صاحبه دين فأرسل إليه رسولاً فقال بعتك الدنانير التي لي عليك بالدراهم التي لك علي وقال قبلت فهو باطل لأن حقوق العقد لا تتعلق بالرسول بل بالمرسل وهما متفرقان بأبدانهما. وكذا لو نادى أحدهما صاحبه من وراء جدار أو ناداه من بعيد لم يجز لأنهما مفترقان بأبدانهما. والمعتبر افتراق المتعاقدين سواء كانا مالكين أو نائبين كالأب والوصي والوكيل لأن القبض من حقوق العقد وحقوقه متعلقه بهما ولا اعتبار بالمجلس إلا في مسألة ما إذا قال الأب اشهدوا أني اشتريت هذا الدينار من ابني الصغير بعشرة دراهم ثم قال قبل أن يزن العشرة فهو باطل؛ كذا روي عن محمد لأن الأب هو العاقد فلا يمكن اعتبار التفرق بالأبدان فيعتبر المجلس؛ كذا في البدائع. وفي الذخيرة لو وكل وكيلين في الصرف فتصارفا ثم ذهب أحدهما قبل القبض وقبض الآخر بطل في حصة الذاهب فقط كالمالكين إذا قبض أحدهما ولم يقبض الآخر بخلاف الوكيلين بقبض الدين إذا قبض أحدهما دون الآخر لم يجز؛ كذا في الذخيرة. وتفرع على اشتراط القبض أنه لا يجوز الإبراء عن بدل الصرف ولا وهي.
As for mutual possession, it means possession before separation by their bodies, such that one takes in one direction and the other in another...
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the condition of possession (qabd) and separation (iftiraq). The author defines taqabud as physical taking before the parties separate by their bodies. Walking even a mile together is not separation if they are still together. The contract is not invalidated by signs that imply aversion (i'rad), unlike the option of the mukhayyara. Several sub-rulings are derived: if two people owe each other debts and one sends a messenger to conduct a Sarf contract, the contract is void because the rights of the contract attach to the actual parties, not the messenger, and the parties are physically separated. Similarly, calling from behind a wall or from a distance invalidates the contract. The criterion is the physical separation of the contracting parties, whether they are principals or agents (father, executor, agent). An exception: if a father says 'Bear witness that I bought this dinar from my minor son for ten dirhams' before weighing the ten, it is void per Muhammad because the father is the contracting party and physical separation is impossible (the son is minor and in his custody), so the sitting (majlis) is considered. For two agents in Sarf, if one leaves before possession and the other later takes, the contract is void only for the absent agent's share, analogous to two principals where only one takes possession. Special rules apply to agents for debt collection. The condition of possession also precludes remission (ibra') of the counter-value in Sarf.

Key Terms
تقابض (taqābuḍ): Mutual physical taking of the counter-values in a Sarf contract before the parties separate.
افتراق بالأبدان (iftirāq bil-abdān): Physical separation of the contracting parties' bodies, not just moving away from the place.
إعراض (i‘rāḍ): Signs of turning away or aversion; does not nullify the contract in Sarf, unlike in khyar al-mukhayyara.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two parties conduct a Sarf contract. One party then walks a mile but the other follows, and they remain together. According to the Hanafi school, have they separated?
A) Yes, because they are no longer in the original sitting
B) No, because they are still physically together
C) Yes, because walking more than a few steps constitutes separation
D) No, but only if they hold hands

Key Takeaway
A Sarf contract is valid only if both parties physically possess the counter-values before their bodies separate; exceptions are narrowly construed.

The Condition of Hand-to-Hand Exchange (Taqabud) in Sarf
Ruling with proof on taqabud in sarf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of taqabud in sarf when items differ in genus and explain why the Hanafi school holds that it is a condition of continuing validity, not initial conclusion.

Core Idea
In sarf of different genera, hand-to-hand exchange is obligatory; omission voids the contract.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq explains the pivotal condition of taqabud in currency exchange (sarf) when the two items are of different species, such as gold and silver. It clarifies that while equality in weight is not required, immediate physical exchange in the session is mandatory, and it resolves an intra-Hanafi debate over whether taqabud is a condition for the contract's valid conclusion or for its continued validity. Understanding this distinction is essential for determining when the contract is void and how corruption spreads to linked transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for different genera
For sarf involving items of different genera (e.g., gold and silver), the condition is hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) before the parties separate; equality in weight is not required. This is based on the hadith 'hand to hand'.
2
Define qabd (receipt) according to Hanafis
Receipt means physical hand-to-hand exchange (qabd bil-barajim), not constructive possession (takhliyah). This ensures immediate transfer.
Hanafis strictly require physical handover; other schools may accept constructive possession.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the nature of taqabud
Some early Hanafis held that taqabud is a condition for the valid conclusion (inshiqad) of the contract. The correct view is that it is a condition for its continued validity (baqā'), meaning the contract is initially valid but becomes void if separation occurs without receipt.
Imam Muhammad's statement 'if they separate before receipt, it becomes void' supports the baqā' view.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If a sarf contract is combined with another transaction, and the sarf is spoiled due to missing taqabud, the weak view holds that the corruption spreads to the entire contract; the correct view holds that it does not.
This distinction matters in mixed contracts like buying gold and silver plus a commodity.
5
Apply the ruling to special cases
For selling gold for fils (copper coins), only one counter-value needs to be received before separation. For selling gold for silver by lump sum (mujāzafah), the contract is valid if taqabud occurs; if they separate before receipt, it is void.
Lump sum is permissible when genus differs because equality is not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِلَّا شَرْطُ التَّقَابُضِ أَيْ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَتَجَانَسَا يُشْتَرَطُ التَّقَابُضُ قَبْلَ الَافْتِرَاقِ دُونَ التَّمَاثُلِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَاهُ مِنَ الْحَدِيثِ. وَفِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ وَالْمِعْرَاجِ مُعْتَزِياً إِلَى فَوَائِدِ الْقُدُورِيِّ: الْمُرَادُ بِالْقَبْضِ هُنَا الْقَبْضُ بِالْبَرَاجِمِ لَا بِالتَّخْلِيَةِ يُرِيدُ بِالْيَدِ اهـ. ثُمَّ اخْتَلَفُوا فِي الْقَبْضِ فَقِيلَ شَرْطُ انْعِقَادِهِ صَحِيحاً فَأَوْرَدَ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ حِينَئِذٍ لَا بُدَّ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ أَوْ التَّقَدُّمِ وَالْقَبْضُ مُتَأَخِّرٌ فَكَانَ حُكْماً لَهُ لَا شَرْطاً وَأُجِيبَ بِأَنَّ الْوُجُودَ فِي الْمَجْلِسِ جُعِلَ مُقَارِناً لِلْعَقْدِ حُكْماً، وَالصَّحِيحُ الْمُخْتَارُ أَنَّهُ شَرْطُ بَقَائِهِ عَلَى الصِّحَّةِ لَا شَرْطُ انْعِقَادِهِ وَقَدْ أَشَارَ مُحَمَّدٌ إِلَى كُلٍّ مِنْهُمَا كَمَا فِي الذَّخِيرَةِ. وَيَدُلُّ عَلَى الثَّانِي قَوْلُهُ فَإِنْ تَفَرَّقَا قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ بَطَلَ فَلَوْلَا أَنَّهُ مُنْعَقِدٌ لَمَا بَطَلَ بِالَافْتِرَاقِ؛ كَذَا فِي الْمِعْرَاجِ وَثَمَرَةُ الْخِلَافِ تَظْهَرُ فِيمَا إِذَا ظَهَرَ الْفَسَادُ فِيمَا هُوَ صَرْفٌ فَهَلْ يُفْسِدُ فِيمَا لَيْسَ بِصَرْفٍ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ فَعَلَى الْقَوْلِ الضَّعِيفِ يَتَعَدَّى الْفَسَادُ وَعَلَى الْأَصَحِّ لَا يَتَعَدَّى؛ كَذَا فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ. وَقَيَّدَ بِالذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ بَاعَ فِضَّةً بِفُلُوسٍ أَوْ ذَهَبًا بِفُلُوسٍ فَإِنَّهُ يُشْتَرَطُ قَبْضُ أَحَدِ الْبَدَلَيْنِ قَبْلَ الَافْتِرَاقِ لَا قَبْضُهُمَا؛ كَذَا فِي الذَّخِيرَةِ. فَلَوْ بَاعَ الذَّهَبَ بِالْفِضَّةِ مُجَازَفَةً صَحَّ إِنْ تَقَابَضَا فِي الْمَجْلِسِ لِأَنَّ الْمُسْتَحَقَّ هُوَ الْقَبْضُ قَبْلَ الَافْتِرَاقِ دُونَ التَّسْوِيَةِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا فَلَا يَضُرُّهُ الْجُزَافُ وَلَوْ افْتَرَقَا قَبْلَ قَبْضِهِمَا أَوْ قَبْضِ أَحَدِهِمَا بَطَلَ لِفَوَاتِ الشَّرْطِ قَيِّدَ بِبَيْعِ الْجِنْسِ بِخِلَافِ الْجِنْسِ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ بَاعَ الْجِنْسَ بِالْجِنْسِ مُجَازَفَةً فَإِنْ عَلِمَا تَسَاوِيَهُمَا قَبْلَ الَافْتِرَاقِ صَحَّ وَبَعْدَهُ لَا.
And otherwise the condition of mutual receipt: i.e., if they are not of the same genus, mutual receipt before separation is required, not equality, due to the hadith we narrated. In Fath al-Qadir and al-Mi'raj, attributed to Fawa'id al-Quduri: the intended meaning of receipt here is receipt by the knuckles, not by relinquishing; meaning by the hand. End. Then they differed concerning receipt: it was said it is a condition for its valid conclusion. It was objected that then it would require conjunction or precedence while receipt is later, so it would be a ruling for it not a condition. The answer was that existence in the session is made equivalent to conjunction with the contract legally. The correct chosen view is that it is a condition for its remaining valid, not for its conclusion. Muhammad indicated each of them as in al-Dhakhirah. The second is indicated by his statement: if they separate before receipt, it becomes void; for if it were not concluded, separation would not void it. Thus in al-Mi'raj. The fruit of the difference appears when corruption appears in what is sarf: does it corrupt what is not sarf according to Abu Hanifa? According to the weak opinion, the corruption transfers; according to the correct, it does not. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And it is restricted to gold and silver because if he sold silver for fils or gold for fils, the receipt of one of the two counter-values before separation is required, not both. Thus in al-Dhakhirah. So if he sold gold for silver in a lump sum, it is valid if they mutually receive in the session, because what is required is receipt before separation, not equality, due to what we narrated. So lump sum does not harm it. If they separate before receiving both or one of them, it becomes void due to the loss of the condition. It is restricted to selling one genus for another genus because if he sold genus for genus in a lump sum, and they know their equality before separation, it is valid; after it, not.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof discussing the condition of hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) in the contract of sarf (currency exchange). When the two items are of different genera (e.g., gold and silver), equality in weight is not required, but immediate hand-to-hand exchange in the session is mandatory. The text clarifies that 'qabd' (receipt) is by hand (qabd bil-barajim), not by relinquishing (takhliyah). There is a disagreement: is taqabud a condition for the contract's valid conclusion or for its continued validity? The correct view (mu'tamad) is that it is a condition for continued validity, supported by the fact that separation before receipt voids the contract, indicating it was valid initially. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is when sarf is combined with another transaction: if the sarf is spoiled, does it spoil the other? According to the weaker opinion, the corruption spreads; according to the stronger, it does not. The ruling is restricted to gold and silver; for other non-homogeneous items like silver and fils (copper coins), only one of the two counter-values needs to be received before separation. The passage also addresses selling gold for silver in a lump sum (mujazafah): it is valid if hand-to-hand exchange occurs in the session because equality is not required; but if they separate before receipt, it is void. For selling the same genus (e.g., gold for gold) in a lump sum, it is only valid if they know they are equal before separating; otherwise, it is void.

Key Terms
تقابض (taqābuḍ): Hand-to-hand exchange of the two counter-values in the contract session.
مجازفة (mujāzafah): Selling commodities by lump sum without exact measurement or weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is the condition for the validity of a sarf contract when exchanging gold for silver?
A) Equality in weight and hand-to-hand exchange.
B) Hand-to-hand exchange only; equality in weight is not required.
C) Equality in weight only; hand-to-hand exchange is not required.
D) Neither equality nor hand-to-hand exchange is required.

Key Takeaway
Hand-to-hand exchange in the session is an indispensable condition for the validity of a sarf contract, and its absence renders the contract void, even if the genus differs.

Disposal of Price Before Receipt in Sarf (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq)
Examines the ruling against using the price of a sarf contract before receiving it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on disposing of the price in sarf before qabd and evaluate Zufar's dissenting view.

Core Idea
Disposing of the sarf price before receipt is invalid; the subsequent transaction is fasid.

In sarf, each counter-value is considered a price until received. Disposing of the price before qabd is akin to selling before receipt, which is prohibited. This lesson examines the relied-upon Hanafi position and the dissenting view of Imam Zufar, focusing on a common scenario: using the price to buy another item before possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
State the specific act: using the price (e.g., dirhams) of a sarf contract to purchase a cloth before receiving those dirhams. According to the Hanafi school, this act is invalid and the cloth sale is corrupt (fasid).
The ruling applies regardless of mutual consent.
2
State the Hanafi proof
Receipt of the price is a right of Allah (obligatory) and cannot be waived by the parties. Disposal before receipt is like selling the sold item before receipt, which is prohibited by hadith.
This is a haqq Allah, not a haqq al-‘abd.
3
State Zufar's view and proof
Zufar holds that the cloth purchase is valid because monies are not specified in sales. The dirhams used for the cloth are not necessarily the same as the sarf price, so a different set can be used.
This is based on one of two narrations from Zufar.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Receipt of the sarf substitute is obligatory. Substitution (istibdal) would make that obligation futile, so making the cloth's price payable from the sarf substitute is a corrupt condition (shart fasid).
Istibdal is prohibited because it nullifies the right of Allah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: According to Zufar, the cloth sale is valid and the sarf continues. According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, the cloth sale is fasid, and the sarf remains binding (unless the price is wasted, in which case the sarf dissolves).
The majority view is preferred and mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَلَا يَصِحُّ التَّصَرُّفُ فِي ثَمَنِ الصَّرْفِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِهِ فَلَوْ بَاعَ دِينَاراً بِدَرَاهِمَ ثُمَّ اشْتَرَى بِهَا ثَوْباً فَسَدَ بَيْعُ الثَّوْبِ كَقَوْلِنَا اهـ قوله : (وَقَدْ نُقِلَ عَنْ زُفَرَ الْخَ قَالَ فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ : وَهَذَا عَلَى إِحْدَى الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ عَنْهُ أَنَّ النُّقُودَ لَا تَتَعَيَّنُ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ فَأَمَّا عَلَى الرِّوَايَةِ الْأُخْرَى . عَنْهُ فَيَجِبُ أَنْ لَا . وَبِهِ انْدَفَعَ تَرْجِيحُ ابْنِ الْهُمَامِ الْخ فِيهِ نَظَرٌ ظَاهِرٌ فَإِنَّ الْمُحَقِّقَ قَدْ أَجَابَ عَنْ هَذَا وَكَانَ الْمُؤَلِّفُ لَمْ يُكْمِلْ يَصِحُّ بَيْعُ الثَّوْبِ كَقَوْلِنَا اهـ. قوله : (وَقَدْ نُقِلَ عَنْ زُفَرَ الْخ قَالَ فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ : وَهَذَا عَلَى إِحْدَى الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ عَنْهُ أَنَّ النُّقُودَ لَا تَتَعَيَّنُ فِي الْبِيَاعَاتِ فَأَمَّا عَلَى الرِّوَايَةِ الْأُخْرَى . عَنْهُ فَيَجِبُ أَنْ لَا . وَبِهِ انْدَفَعَ تَرْجِيحُ ابْنِ الْهُمَامِ الْخ فِيهِ نَظَرٌ ظَاهِرٌ فَإِنَّ الْمُحَقِّقَ قَدْ أَجَابَ عَنْ هَذَا وَكَانَ الْمُؤَلِّفُ لَمْ يُكْمِلْ ـ وَلَا يَصِحُّ التَّصَرُّفُ فِي ثَمَنِ الصَّرْفِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِهِ فَلَوْ بَاعَ دِينَاراً بِدَرَاهِمَ وَاشْتَرَى بِهَا ثَوْباً فَسَدَ بَيْعُ الثَّوْبِ أَيْ فِي أَحَدِ بَدَلَيْ الصَّرْفِ لِأَنَّ كُلًّا مِنْهُمَا ثَمَنٌ فَلَا تَجُوزُ هِبَتُهُ وَلَا صَدَقَتُهُ وَلَا بَيْعُ شَيْءٍ بِهِ، وَقَدَّمْنَا أَنَّهُ إِنْ وَهَبَ أَوْ تَصَدَّقَ بِهِ أَوْ أَبْرَأَهُ فَإِنْ قَبِلَ الْآخَرُ انْفَسَخَ الصَّرْفُ لِتَعَذُّرِ وُجُودِ الْقَبْضِ وَإِلَّا فَلَا. وَأَمَّا الْبَيْعُ فَصُورَتُهُ كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ بَاعَ دِينَاراً بِعَشَرَةِ دَرَاهِمَ وَلَمْ يَقْبِضْهَا حَتَّى اشْتَرَى بِهَا ثَوْباً أَوْ مَكِيلًا أَوْ مَوْزُوناً فَالْبَيْعُ فِي الثَّوْبِ فَاسِدٌ لِأَنَّ قَبْضَ الْعَشَرَةِ مُسْتَحَقٌّ حَقَّ اللهِ تَعَالَى فَلَا يَسْقُطُ بِإِسْقَاطِ الْمُتَعَاقِدَيْنِ فَلَمْ يَجُزْ بَيْعُ الثَّوْبِ وَالصَّرْفُ عَلَى حَالِهِ يُقْبِضُ بَدَلَهُ مِنْ عَاقِدِهِ مَعَهُ وَأُورِدَ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّ فَسَادَ الصَّرْفِ حِينَئِذٍ حَقُّ اللهِ تَعَالَى وَصِحَّةُ الثَّوْبِ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ فَتَعَارَضَا فَيُقَدَّمُ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ لِتَفَضُّلِ اللهِ بِذَلِكَ وَأُجِيبَ بِأَنَّ ذَلِكَ بَعْدَ ثُبُوتِ الْحَقَّيْنِ وَلَمْ يَثْبُتْ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ بَعْدُ لِأَنَّهُ يَفُوتُ حَقَّ اللهِ بَعْدَ تَحَقُّقِهِ فَيَمْتَنِعُ لَا أَنَّهُ يَرْتَفِعُ، وَقَدْ نُقِلَ عَنْ زُفَرَ صِحَّةُ بَيْعِ الثَّوْبِ لِأَنَّ الثَّمَنَ فِي بَيْعِهِ لَمْ يَتَعَيَّنْ كَوْنُهُ بَدَلَ الصَّرْفِ لِأَنَّ الْعَقْدَ لَا يَتَعَيَّنُ فَإِضَافَةُ الْعَقْدِ إِلَى بَدَلِ الصَّرْفِ كَعَدَمِ إِضَافَتِهِ فَيَجُوزُ شِرَاءُ ثَوْبٍ بِدَرَاهِمَ لَمْ يُصِفْهَا. وَجَوَابُهُ أَنَّ قَبْضَ بَدَلِ الصَّرْفِ وَاجِبٌ وَالِاسْتِبْدَالُ يُفَوِّتُهُ فَكَانَ شَرْطَ إِيفَاءِ ثَمَنِ الثَّوْبِ مِنْ بَدَلِ الصَّرْفِ شَرْطاً فَاسِداً فَيَمْتَنِعُ الْجَوَازُ وَقَدْ رَجَّحَهُ فِي فَتْحِ الْقَدِيرِ. ثُمَّ اعْلَمْ أَنَّهُمْ قَرَّرُوا هُنَا كَمَا فِي الْمِعْرَاجِ أَنَّ الْبَدَلَيْنِ فِي بَابِ الصَّرْفِ كُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا ثَمَنٌ قَبْلَ الْعَقْدِ وَمَثْمَنٌ مِنْ وَجْهٍ بَعْدَ الْعَقْدِ ضَرُورَةَ أَنَّ الْعَقْدَ لَا يَخْلُو مِنْ مَثْمَنٍ فَلَا يَجُوزُ الِاسْتِبْدَالُ بِأَحَدِهِمَا قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ لِكَوْنِهِ بَيْعَ الْمَبِيعِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِهِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ، وَبِهِ انْدَفَعَ تَرْجِيحُ ابْنِ الْهُمَامِ قَوْلَ زُفَرَ كَمَا لَا يَخْفَى. وَفِي الذَّخِيرَةِ إِذَا اشْتَرَى الرَّجُلُ أَلْفَ دِرْهَمٍ بِعَيْنِهَا بِمِائَةِ دِينَارٍ وَالدَّرَاهِمُ بِيضٌ فَأَعْطَاهُ مَكَانَهَا سُوداً وَرَضِيَ بِهَا الْبَائِعُ جَازَ ذَلِكَ لِأَنَّ هَذَا لَيْسَ بِاسْتِبْدَالٍ وَالسُّودُ وَالْبِيضُ مِنَ الدَّرَاهِمِ جِنْسٌ وَاحِدٌ، وَإِنَّمَا أَبْرَأَهُ عَنْ صِفَةِ الْجَوْدَةِ حِينَ تَجَوَّزَ بِالسُودِ فَكَانَ مُسْتَوْفِياً بِهَذِهِ الطَّرِيقِ لَا مُسْتَبْدِلاً . قَالَ شَمْسُ الْأَئِمَّةِ السَّرَخْسِيُّ: وَمُرَادُهُ مِنْ السُّودِ الدَّرَاهِمُ الْمَضْرُوبَةُ مِنَ النُّقُودِ السُّودِ لَا الدَّرَاهِمُ الْبُخَارِيَّةُ لِأَنَّ أَخْذَ الْبُخَارِيَّةِ مَكَانَ الدَّرَاهِمِ الْبِيضِ لَا يَجُوزُ لِأَنَّهُ يَكُونُ اسْتِبْدَالاً لِاخْتِلَافِ الْجِنْسِ. وَكَذَلِكَ لَوْ قَبَضَ مُشْتَرِي الدَّرَاهِمِ الدَّرَاهِمَ فَأَرَادَ أَنْ يُعْطِيَ ضَرْباً آخَرَ مِنَ الدَّنَانِيرِ سِوَى مَا شَرَطَ لَا يَجُوزُ إِلَّا بِرِضَا صَاحِبِهِ وَإِذَا رَضِيَ بِهِ صَاحِبُهُ كَانَ مُسْتَوْفِياً لَا مُسْتَبْدِلًا لِكَوْنِ الْجِنْسِ وَاحِداً. قِيلَ : هَذَا إِذَا أَعْطَى ضَرْباً دُونَ الْمُسَمَّى، فَأَمَّا إِذَا أَعْطَاهُ ضَرْباً فَوْقَ الْمُسَمَّى فَلَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى رِضَا صَاحِبِهِ اهـ . وَقَدَّمْنَا جَوَازَ الرَّهْنِ بِبَدَلِ الصَّرْفِ فَإِنْ هَلَكَ وَهُمَا فِي الْمَجْلِسِ هَلَكَ بِمَا فِيهِ وَجَازَ الْعَقْدُ، وَإِنَّ النَّظَرَ فِي عِبَارَتِهِ، ثُمَّ رَأَيْتُ صَاحِبَ النَّهْرِ لَخَّصَ جَوَابَ الْمُحَقِّقِ وَاعْتَرَضَ كَلَامَ الْمُؤَلِّفِ حَيْثُ قَالَ : وَلَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ زُفَرَ إِنَّمَا قَالَ يَجُوزُ الْبَيْعُ بِنَاءً عَلَى عَدَمِ تَعَيُّنِ بَدَلِ الصَّرْفِ ثَمَناً فَجَازَ أَنْ يُعْطِيَ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ، وَلَا شَكَّ أَنَّهُ يَقُولُ بِعَدَمِ جَوَازِ بَيْعِ الْمَبِيعِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ فَإِذَا قَالَ بِصِحَّةِ هَذَا الْبَيْعِ لِمَا قُلْنَا كَانَ بِالضَّرُورَةِ قَائِماً بِأَنَّ الْبَيْعَ انْعَقَدَ مُوجِباً دَفْعَ مِثْلِهِ وَتَكُونُ تَسْمِيَتُهُ بَدَلَ الصَّرْفِ تَقْدِيراً لِلثَّمَنِ، سَوَاءٌ سَمَّيْتَهُ بَيْعاً أَوْ
His statement: (And disposing of the price of sarf before its receipt is not valid. If he sold a dinar for dirhams then bought a cloth with them, the sale of the cloth becomes corrupt, as per our statement. End) His statement: (And it has been transmitted from Zufar...) He said in Fath al-Qadir: This is according to one of the two narrations from him that monies are not specified in sales; as for the other narration, it must not. With this, the tarjih of Ibn al-Humam is repelled, but there is apparent consideration in it; indeed the muhaqqiq answered this, and the author did not complete... (And he said: And disposing of the price of sarf before its receipt is not valid. If he sold a dinar for dirhams and bought a cloth with them, the sale of the cloth becomes corrupt, i.e., in one of the two counter-values of sarf, because each of them is a price. So neither gifting nor giving charity nor selling anything with it is permissible. And we have mentioned that if he gifted or gave charity with it or remitted it, if the other accepts, the sarf is dissolved because of the impossibility of receipt; otherwise not. As for the sale, its form is as the author mentioned: sold a dinar for ten dirhams and did not receive them until he bought a cloth or a measurable or weighable item with them; the sale of the cloth is corrupt because receipt of the ten is a right of Allah, so it cannot be dropped by the mutual dropping of the two contractors, so selling the cloth is not permissible, and the sarf remains in its state; he receives its substitute from his counterpart. And it was objected that the corruption of the sarf then is a right of Allah, and the validity of the cloth is a right of the slave, so they conflict, and the right of the slave is given precedence because Allah is gracious in that. The answer was that that is after the two rights have been established, and the right of the slave has not yet been established because it would make the right of Allah futile after its realization, so it is prevented, not that it is raised. And it has been transmitted from Zufar the validity of buying the cloth because the price in his sale is not specified as being the substitute of sarf because the contract does not specify; so adding the contract to the substitute of sarf is like not adding to it, so it is permissible to buy a cloth with dirhams he has not specified. Its answer is that receipt of the substitute of sarf is obligatory, and substitution makes it futile, so making payment of the price of the cloth from the substitute of sarf a condition is a corrupt condition, so permissibility is prevented, and it is preferred in Fath al-Qadir. Then know that they have established here as in al-Mi'raj that the two counter-values in the chapter of sarf are each a price before the contract and a commodity in a sense after the contract, necessarily because a contract cannot be without a commodity. So substitution with one of them before receipt is not permissible because it is selling the sold item before receipt. And with this the tarjih of Ibn al-Humam for the statement of Zufar is repelled, as is not hidden. In al-Dhakhirah: If a man buys one thousand specific dirhams for one hundred dinars, and the dirhams are white, so he gave him black ones instead and the seller was pleased, that is permitted because this is not a substitution, and black and white dirhams are one genus. He only released him from the quality of goodness when he accepted the black ones, so he was receiving in this way, not substituting. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: The intended from black dirhams is the dirhams minted from black coins, not Bukhari dirhams, because taking Bukhari dirhams in place of white dirhams is not permitted because it would be a substitution due to difference of genus. Similarly, if the buyer of dirhams received the dirhams and wanted to give another type of dinars other than what was stipulated, it is not permitted except with the consent of its owner; and if its owner agrees, he is receiving, not substituting, because the genus is one. It was said: This is if he gives a type inferior to what was specified; as for if he gives a type superior to what was specified, there is no need for the consent of its owner. End. And we have earlier discussed the permissibility of pledging with the substitute of sarf; if it perishes while they are in the session, it perishes with what is in it and the contract is valid. There is consideration in his wording. Then I saw the author of al-Nahr summarized the answer of the muhaqqiq and objected to the statement of the author where he said: It is not hidden that Zufar only said the sale is permissible based on the non-specification of the substitute of sarf as a price, so it is permissible to give from other than it. There is no doubt that he says the impermissibility of selling the sold item before receipt. So when he says the validity of this sale due to what we said, he is necessarily stating that the sale was contracted to obligate the delivery of its like, and its being called substitute of sarf is an estimate of the price, whether you call it a sale or...
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling on disposing of the price (thaman) of a sarf contract before taking possession (qabd). The relied-upon Hanafi position is that any disposal – whether gift, charity, sale, or remission – of the price before receipt is invalid, and if one does so (e.g., selling a dinar for ten dirhams and then buying a cloth with those dirhams before receiving them), the subsequent transaction (buying the cloth) is also corrupt (fasid). The reason is that receipt of the price in sarf is a right of Allah (obligatory by divine command) and cannot be waived by the parties. An objection is raised: if the sarf becomes corrupt due to failure of receipt (a haqq Allah), why does that spoil the cloth sale (a haqq al-‘abd)? The answer is that the right of the slave (the validity of the cloth purchase) is conditional upon the existence of a valid price, which is not established because the price is still owed to the seller from the sarf. Imam Zufar dissented, arguing that because monies are not specified (mut'aayin) in sales, the dirhams used to buy the cloth are not necessarily the same as the price of the sarf. Therefore, one could use other dirhams to pay for the cloth, and the purchase is valid. The Hanafi response is that receipt of the sarf substitute is obligatory and any substitution (istibdal) frustrates that obligation; thus, making the cloth’s price payable from the sarf substitute is a corrupt condition (shart fāsid). The passage then clarifies the principle: both counter-values in sarf are considered price (thaman) before the contract and commodity (muthman) in a sense after the contract, so disposing of either before receipt is akin to selling the sold item before receipt (bay' al-mabī‘ qabla qabḍih), which is prohibited. This refutes Ibn al-Humam's leaning toward Zufar's view. Additional examples are given: if a buyer of white dirhams accepts black dirhams with the seller's consent, it is valid because it is not a substitution but a renegotiation of quality within the same genus; similarly, if the buyer wishes to give a different type of dinar after receipt, it requires the seller's consent unless it is of superior quality. The passage ends with a discussion of pledging (rahn) the substitute of sarf.

Key Terms
ثمن الصرف (thaman al-sarf): One of the two counter-values in a sarf contract; each is considered a price (thaman) and cannot be disposed of before receipt.
استبدال (istibdāl): Substituting one of the counter-values with a different item before possession, which is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the status of buying a cloth with the dirhams that are the price of a sarf contract before the dirhams are received?
A) The cloth purchase is valid if the seller agrees.
B) The cloth purchase is valid because the dirhams are not specified.
C) The cloth purchase is corrupt (fasid) and the sarf is dissolved if receipt becomes impossible.
D) The cloth purchase is corrupt (fasid) but the sarf contract remains binding.

Key Takeaway
In sarf, each counter-value is a price; disposing of it before receipt is invalid, and any transaction based on that price is corrupt, even if the other contracting party agrees.

Redirecting Genus to Opposite Genus to Validate a Sarf Contract
Explaining the Hanafi principle of redirecting genus in mixed sarf contracts with objections and replies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of sarraf al-jins ila khilaf jinsihi to validate a mixed sarf contract and defend it against objections.

Core Idea
In mixed sarf, the law redirects each genus to its opposite, avoiding riba by smallest change.

Hanafi jurists employ a creative method to salvage mixed currency exchanges that would otherwise fall into riba: redirecting each item to its correct genus. This lesson examines the principle of 'sarraf al-jins' as explained by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, along with objections and answers. You will learn how this principle is derived and why it is considered the minimal intervention.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: a mixed sarf contract (e.g., dirham + garment for another dirham + garment) is valid by redirecting each item to its opposite genus to avoid riba.
The redirection is a form of tashih al-aqd (contract correction).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that some object: multiple possible redirections make the correction arbitrary.
The opponent may be from other schools or even a hypothetical critic.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The objection: it's possible to redirect the dinar to the dinar and dirham to dirham, or dinar to dirham, etc., so the choice is not determined.
This challenges the certainty of the correction.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi reply: the smallest change is chosen, i.e., redirecting only as necessary to avoid riba. This is analogous to selling half of a jointly owned slave.
The principle is derived from qiyas and istihsan.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi law validates such contracts; other schools may invalidate them unless each item is explicitly paired.
This shows how the same facts can produce different rulings.

مقايلاً بخلاف جنسه تصحيحاً للعقد، ولو صرف إلى جنس مفسد لأن العقد يقتضي مطلق المقابلة من غير تعرض لقيد لا مقابلة الكل بالكل شائعاً ولا فرداً معيناً فصار كما لو باع نصف عبد مشترك بينه وبين غيره فإنه ينصرف إلى نصيبه تصحيحاً للعقد وكانصراف النقد إلى المتعارف، ولا يرد علينا ما لو اشترى قلباً بعشرة وثوباً بعشرة ثم باعهما مرابحة بخمسة وعشرين فإنه لا يصح وإن أمكن صرف الربح إلى الثوب لأنا لو صرفناه لصار تولية في القلب وهو خلاف المرابحة فكان إبطالاً له. وكذا لا يرد لو اشترى عبداً بألف ثم باعه قبل النقد مع آخر من البائع بألف وخمسمائة فإنه لا يصح في المشتري بألف لأن طريق التصحيح غیر متعين لإمكان صرف الألف ومائة إليه أو مائتين إلى غير ذلك من الصورة. وأورد عليه أن الطرق متعددة في مسألة الكتاب لجواز أن يصرف الدينار إلى الدينار والدرهم إلى الدرهم والدينار إلى الدرهم كما يجوز أن يصرف الدرهمان إلى الدينارين والدينار إلى الدرهم. وأجيب بأنه أقل تغييراً فكان أولى وكذا لا يرد علينا ما لو جمع بين عبده وعبد غيره وقال بعتك أحدهما فإنه لا يصح للتنكير وإن أمكن تصحيحه بصرفه إلى عبده وأجيب بأن البيع أضيف إلى منكر فلا ينصرف إلى المعين للتضاد إذا المنكر ليس بمحل للبيع. ورد بأنه يسن بشيء لأن المعرفة مما صدقات النكرة فإن زيداً يصدق عليه رجل ولا شك أنه يحتمله فيجب حمله عليه . وقد قال أبو حنيفة في قوله عبدي أو حماري حر أنه يعتق العبد ويجعل استعارة المنكر للمعرف، وكذا ما قيل إن تصحيح العقد يجب في محل العقد وهو لم يضف إلى المعين. وفي فتح القدير: واعلم أن ما أورد على دفع النقوض المذكورة أن الحظ له جواب فذاك وإلا فلا يضرك النقض في إثبات المطلوب إذ غايته أنه خطأ في محل آخر إذا اعترف بخطؤه في محل النقض وذلك لا يوجب خطأه في محل النزاع .اهـ.
Corresponding to opposite genus to correct the contract. And if he directs it to a corrupt genus, because the contract necessitates absolute correspondence without conditioning a restriction, not a whole-to-whole exchange as a common share nor a specified individual, so it becomes like selling half of a jointly owned slave between him and another, for it is directed to his share to correct the contract, and similarly the direction of cash to the customary. And the following does not refute us: if someone buys a heart for ten and a garment for ten, then sells them at a profit for twenty-five, it is not valid even if it is possible to attribute the profit to the garment, because if we attribute it, it would become a wala' in the heart, contradicting the profit sale, thus invalidating it. Similarly, it is not refuted if someone buys a slave for one thousand, then sells it before payment together with another from the seller for one thousand five hundred, it is not valid in the buyer for one thousand because the path of correction is not determined due to the possibility of attributing one thousand and one hundred to it or two hundred, etc. It was objected that the paths are multiple in the book's issue: it is permissible to direct the dinar to the dinar and the dirham to the dirham and the dinar to the dirham, as it is permissible to direct two dirhams to the two dinars and the dinar to the dirham. The answer was: it is the smallest change so it is better. Similarly, the following does not refute us: if someone combined his slave and another's slave and said 'I sell you one of them,' it is not valid due to indefiniteness, even if correction is possible by directing it to his slave. The answer was: the sale is attached to an indefinite, so it is not directed to the definite due to contradiction, since the indefinite is not a subject for sale. It was responded that it is permissible [according to some] because the definite is among the referents of the indefinite, for Zayd is described as a man, and there is no doubt that it can apply to him, so it must be interpreted accordingly. And Abu Hanifa said in the statement 'my slave or my donkey is free' that the slave is freed, making the indefinite a metaphor for the definite. Similarly, what was said: 'The correction of the contract must be in the subject of the contract, and he did not attach it to the definite.' In Fath al-Qadir: Know that the objection raised against repelling the aforementioned rebuttals is that if one has a good answer, then so be it; otherwise, the rebuttal does not harm you in proving the desired, for at most it is an error in another place, and if one acknowledges his error in the place of the rebuttal, that does not necessitate his error in the place of dispute. End.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the Hanafi principle of sarraf al-jins ila khilaf jinsihi (redirecting genus to opposite genus) to validate a sarf (currency exchange) contract that would otherwise involve riba. The author explains that when a contract involves a mix of items (e.g., a dirham and a garment for a dirham and a garment), the law directs the exchange to the opposite genus (e.g., dirham for dirham, garment for garment) to avoid riba. The text defends Abu Hanifa's position by refuting several objections. The first analogy is to selling half of a jointly owned slave, which is directed to the seller's share to validate the sale. The second point relates to directing cash to what is customary. Potential counterexamples are addressed: a profit sale on a heart and garment is invalid because attributing the profit to the garment would make the heart a wala' (trust) transaction, contradicting the profit sale nature. Similarly, a sale of a slave before payment with another item is invalid due to indeterminacy. An objection that multiple directions are possible is answered by choosing the smallest change. Another objection about selling one of two slaves (one owned, one not) is answered by noting that the sale is attached to an indefinite noun, which cannot be directed to a definite. A rebuttal citing Abu Hanifa's ruling on manumission (where 'my slave or my donkey is free' results in the slave being freed) is addressed by distinguishing contexts. The passage concludes with a quote from Fath al-Qadir emphasizing that objections in other contexts do not undermine the principle at hand. This is a classic Hanafi argument using qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) to validate mixed contracts.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): The exchange of gold, silver, or currency, with specific rules against riba.
تصحيح العقد (tashih al-aqd): The act of interpreting or redirecting the contract's terms to make it valid under shari'ah.
جنس (jins): Genus or category, especially for riba items (gold, silver, wheat, etc.)
مقابلة (muqabila): Counterpart or consideration in an exchange contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, when a sarf contract involves mixed items (e.g., a dirham and a garment for a dirham and a garment), what principle is used to validate the contract?
A) It is always invalid
B) The contract is corrected by redirecting each genus to its opposite
C) The contract must be nullified
D) The parties must repeat the exchange in separate transactions

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law validates mixed sarf contracts by redirecting each genus to its opposite, choosing the smallest change to avoid riba.

Dirham and Garment Exchange: Invalidity Due to Parting Without Possession
Clarifying that a sarf contract is initially valid but becomes invalid when parties part without possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a sarf contract when parties part without possession and distinguish between initial validity and supervening corruption.

Core Idea
Parting without possession in a mixed sarf contract causes supervening corruption, voiding the exchange.

You may think that any irregularity in an exchange makes it invalid from the start. The Hanafi school, however, distinguishes between original defects and those that arise after a valid contract. This lesson examines a specific case: buying a dirham and a garment together for another dirham and garment, then separating before taking possession. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying sarf rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
The transaction involves dirham (currency) and garment (commodity) on both sides. This is a composite contract combining sarf (currency exchange) and a regular sale.
The dirham-dirham portion is sarf; the garment-garment portion is ordinary sale.
2
Determine initial validity
The author states the contract was concluded validly. Why? Because the mixed nature allows redirecting the genus (sarf) to avoid riba, making it sound at inception.
The principle of 'redirecting genus' applies only at contract formation.
3
Identify the supervening defect
The parties separated (iftiraq) without taking possession (qabd) of the dirhams. In sarf, possession before parting is required; violation after valid formation introduces 'fasad tari'' (supervening corruption).
This is not an original flaw but a condition violated post-contract.
4
Apply the ruling from al-Mabsut
The cited fatwa: if they part before possession, the dirham contract is void (batal). The garment part may remain valid if separable, but the sarf portion is null.
Void (batil) here likely means the entire contract becomes fasid (corrupt) as per Hanafi terminology.
5
Contrast stratagem (hila) usage
A stratagem can validate a contract at inception but cannot maintain validity after corruption. Once the defect occurs, it cannot be cured.
This highlights the school's strictness on possession in sarf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما مسألة ما إذا باع درهماً وثوباً بدرهم وثوب وافترقا بلا قبض فليس مما نحن فيه فإن العقد انعقد صحيحاً، وإنما طرأ الفساد بالافتراق والصرف لدفع الفساد وقد انعقد بلا فساد وكلامنا ليس في الفساد الطارئ. وفي الظهيرية معزياً إلى المبسوط : باع عشرة وثوباً بعشرة وثوب وافترقا قبل القبض بطل العقد الدراهم ولو صرف الجنس إلى خلاف جنسه لم يبطل ولكن قيل في العقود يحتال للتصحيح في الابتداء ولا يحتال للبقاء على الصحة اهـ.
As for the issue when he sold a dirham and a garment for a dirham and a garment and they separated without possession, it is not from what we are in; for the contract was concluded validly, and corruption only occurred through separation, and sarf is to repel corruption, and it was concluded without corruption, and our speech is not about supervening corruption. In al-Zahiriyyah, citing al-Mabsut: He sold ten and a garment for ten and a garment and they separated before possession; the contract of the dirhams became void. And if he directed the genus to opposite genus, it would not become void. But it is said in contracts: one may use stratagem for correction at the beginning, but not for maintaining validity. End.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage addresses the status of a sarf contract where a dirham and a garment are exchanged for a dirham and a garment, and the parties separate without taking possession. The author clarifies that such a contract is initially valid because it is a mixed exchange that can be corrected by the principle of redirecting genus. However, if they part without taqabud (possession), the contract becomes corrupt (fasid) due to the supervening defect. The ruling from al-Mabsut is cited: if they part before possession, the contract of the dirhams is void, even though the genus could be redirected to avoid riba. The text notes a subtle difference: one may use a stratagem (hila) to validate a contract at its inception, but not to maintain its validity after corruption. This highlights the Hanafi emphasis on immediate possession in sarf contracts.

Key Terms
افتراق (iftiraq): The physical separation of parties after a contract; in sarf, it nullifies the contract if without prior possession.
فساد طارئ (fasad tari'): Supervening corruption that occurs after a valid contract due to a violation of a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if two parties exchange a dirham and a garment for a dirham and a garment and then separate without taking possession, what is the ruling?
A) The contract is void from the start
B) The contract is valid and remains valid
C) The contract is initially valid but becomes corrupt due to separation
D) The contract is valid if they had intended possession later

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a sarf contract is initially valid if the genus can be redirected, but parting without possession introduces supervening corruption, voiding the currency exchange.
